<p>Hyena biologists protested against the animal's portrayal: one hyena researcher sued Disney studios for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defamation_of_character" title="Defamation of character">defamation of character</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> and another—who had organized the animators' visit to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California</a>'s Field Station for Behavioural Research, where they would observe and sketch captive hyenas—<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-glick_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-glick-108">[108]</a></sup> included <a href="/wiki/Boycott" title="Boycott">boycotting</a> <i>The Lion King</i> among the ways it would help preserve hyenas in the wild.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The hyenas have also been interpreted to represent an anti-immigrant allegory, where the hyenas would be black and Latino ethnic communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The film has also been criticised for advancing a fascist narrative in its portrayal of the lion kingdom and the circle of life where "only the strong and the beautiful triumph, and the powerless survive only by serving the strong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels_and_spin-offs">Sequels and spin-offs</span></h3>
<p>The first <i>Lion King</i>-related animated projects involved the characters of Timon and Pumbaa. First, the duo starred in the animated short "Stand by Me", featuring Timon singing <a href="/wiki/Stand_by_Me_(song)" title="Stand by Me (song)">the eponymous song</a>, which was released in 1995 accompanying the theatrical release of <i><a href="/wiki/Tom_and_Huck" title="Tom and Huck">Tom and Huck</a></i>. Then the duo received their own animated show, <i><a href="/wiki/Timon_%26_Pumbaa_(TV_series)" title="Timon &amp; Pumbaa (TV series)">The Lion King's Timon and Pumbaa</a></i>, which ran for three seasons and 85 episodes between 1995 and 1999. Ernie Sabella continued to voice Pumbaa, while Timon was voiced by <a href="/wiki/Quinton_Flynn" title="Quinton Flynn">Quinton Flynn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Schon" title="Kevin Schon">Kevin Schon</a> in addition to Nathan Lane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>Disney released two direct-to-video films related to <i>The Lion King</i>. The first was sequel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_II:_Simba%27s_Pride" title="The Lion King II: Simba's Pride">The Lion King II: Simba's Pride</a></i>, issued in 1998 on VHS. The film centers around Simba and Nala's daughter, Kiara, who falls in love with Kovu, a male lion who was raised in a pride of Scar's followers, the Outsiders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> 2004 saw the release of another <i>Lion King</i> film on DVD, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_1%C2%BD" title="The Lion King 1½">The Lion King 1½</a></i>. It is a prequel in showing how Timon and Pumbaa met each other, and also a <a href="/wiki/Sequel#Parallel" title="Sequel">parallel</a> in that it also depicts what the characters were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retconned" title="Retconned">retconned</a> to have done during the events of the original movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2014, it was announced that a new TV series based on the film would be released called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_Guard" title="The Lion Guard">The Lion Guard</a></i>, featuring Kion, the second-born cub of Simba and Nala. <i>The Lion Guard</i> is a sequel to <i>The Lion King</i> and takes place during the time-gap within <i>The Lion King II: Simba's Pride.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> It was first broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Disney_Channel" title="Disney Channel">Disney Channel</a> as a television film titled <i>The Lion Guard: Return of the Roar</i> in November 2015 before airing as a series on <a href="/wiki/Disney_Junior" title="Disney Junior">Disney Junior</a> in January 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live-action_adaptation">Live-action adaptation</span></h3>
<p>In September 2016, following the critical and financial success of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jungle_Book_(2016_film)" title="The Jungle Book (2016 film)">The Jungle Book</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Walt Disney Pictures</a> announced that they were developing a <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> created live-action remake of <i>The Lion King</i>, with <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a> directing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-favreau_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-favreau-121">[121]</a></sup> Favreau will shoot it back to back with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Jungle_Book_(2016_film)#Sequel" title="The Jungle Book (2016 film)">The Second Jungle Book</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-favreau_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-favreau-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(video_game)" title="The Lion King (video game)">The Lion King (video game)</a></div>
<p>Along with the film release, three different video games based on <i>The Lion King</i> were released by <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Interactive" title="Virgin Interactive">Virgin Interactive</a> in December 1994. The main title was developed by <a href="/wiki/Westwood_Studios" title="Westwood Studios">Westwood Studios</a>, and published for <a href="/wiki/Personal_computer" title="Personal computer">PC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amiga" title="Amiga">Amiga</a> computers and the consoles <a href="/wiki/Super_Nintendo_Entertainment_System" title="Super Nintendo Entertainment System">SNES</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sega_Mega_Drive" title="Sega Mega Drive">Sega Mega Drive/Genesis</a>. Dark Technologies created the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy" title="Game Boy">Game Boy</a> version, while Syrox Developments handled the <a href="/wiki/Master_System" title="Master System">Master System</a> and <a href="/wiki/Game_Gear" title="Game Gear">Game Gear</a> version.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> The film and sequel <i>Simba's Pride</i> later inspired another game, <a href="/wiki/Torus_Games" title="Torus Games">Torus Games</a>' <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King:_Simba%27s_Mighty_Adventure" title="The Lion King: Simba's Mighty Adventure">The Lion King: Simba's Mighty Adventure</a></i> (2000) for the <a href="/wiki/Game_Boy_Color" title="Game Boy Color">Game Boy Color</a> and <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Timon and Pumbaa also appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Timon_%26_Pumbaa%27s_Jungle_Games" title="Timon &amp; Pumbaa's Jungle Games">Timon &amp; Pumbaa's Jungle Games</a></i>, a 1995 PC game collection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puzzle_game" title="Puzzle game">puzzle games</a> by <a href="/wiki/7th_Level" title="7th Level">7th Level</a>, later ported to the SNES by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tiertex" title="Tiertex">Tiertex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Square_Enix" title="Square Enix">Square Enix</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hearts" title="Kingdom Hearts">Kingdom Hearts</a></i> features Simba as a recurring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gameplay_of_Final_Fantasy#Magic" title="Gameplay of Final Fantasy">summon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KH-StrategyGuide_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-KH-StrategyGuide-126">[126]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> as well as a playable in the <i>Lion King</i> world, known as Pride Lands, in <i><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_Hearts_II" title="Kingdom Hearts II">Kingdom Hearts II</a></i>. There the plotline is loosely related to the later part of the original film, with all of the main characters except Zazu and Sarabi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup> <i>The Lion King</i> also provides one of the worlds featured in the 2011 action-adventure game <i><a href="/wiki/Disney_Universe" title="Disney Universe">Disney Universe</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> and Simba was featured in the <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a> title <i><a href="/wiki/Disney_Friends" title="Disney Friends">Disney Friends</a></i> (2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stage_adaptations">Stage adaptations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)">The Lion King (musical)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg"><img alt="The façade of Minskoff Theatre at Broadway, with banners promoting the Lion King musical." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="642" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/150px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/225px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg/300px-Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Il_Re_Leone_Insegne_in_Time_Square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Advertisements for the musical adaptation of <i>The Lion King</i> at <a href="/wiki/Minskoff_Theatre" title="Minskoff Theatre">Minskoff Theatre</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Disney_Theatrical_Productions" title="Disney Theatrical Productions">Walt Disney Theatrical</a> produced a musical stage adaptation of the same name, which premiered in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minneapolis,_Minnesota" title="Minneapolis, Minnesota">Minneapolis, Minnesota</a> in July 1997, and later opened on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_theatre" title="Broadway theatre">Broadway</a> in October 1997 at the <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam_Theatre" title="New Amsterdam Theatre">New Amsterdam Theatre</a>. <a href="/wiki/The_Lion_King_(musical)" title="The Lion King (musical)"><i>The Lion King</i> musical</a> was directed by <a href="/wiki/Julie_Taymor" title="Julie Taymor">Julie Taymor</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> and featured songs from both the movie and <i>Rhythm of the Pride Lands</i>, along with three new compositions by Elton John and Tim Rice. Mark Mancina did the musical arrangements and new orchestral tracks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> The musical became one of the most successful in Broadway history, winning six <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tony_Awards" title="Tony Awards">Tony Awards</a> including <a href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical" title="Tony Award for Best Musical">Best Musical</a>, and despite moving to the <a href="/wiki/Minskoff_Theatre" title="Minskoff Theatre">Minskoff Theatre</a> in 2006, is still running to this day in New York, becoming the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_longest-running_Broadway_shows" title="List of the longest-running Broadway shows">third longest-running show</a> and highest grossing Broadway production in history. The show's financial success led to adaptations all over the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schu_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-schu-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>The Lion King</i> inspired two attractions retelling the story of the film at <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Parks_and_Resorts" title="Walt Disney Parks and Resorts">Walt Disney Parks and Resorts</a>. The first, "<a href="/wiki/The_Legend_of_the_Lion_King" title="The Legend of the Lion King">The Legend of the Lion King</a>", featured a recreation of the film through life-size puppets of its characters, and ran from 1994 to 2002 at <a href="/wiki/Magic_Kingdom" title="Magic Kingdom">Magic Kingdom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_World" title="Walt Disney World">Walt Disney World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> Another that is still running is the live-action 30-minute musical revue of the movie, "<a href="/wiki/Festival_of_the_Lion_King" title="Festival of the Lion King">Festival of the Lion King</a>", which incorporates the musical numbers into gymnastic routines with live actors, along with animatronic puppets of Simba and Pumba and a costumed actor as Timon. The attraction opened in April 1998 at Disney World's <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney's Animal Kingdom">Animal Kingdom</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> and in September 2005 in <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong_Disneyland" title="Hong Kong Disneyland">Hong Kong Disneyland</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Adventureland_(Disney)" title="Adventureland (Disney)">Adventureland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> A similar version under the name "The Legend of the Lion King" was featured in <a href="/wiki/Disneyland_Paris" title="Disneyland Paris">Disneyland Paris</a> from 2004 to 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row" style="padding-left:0;padding-right:0;">
<div style="padding:0em 0.75em;">Methods and<br/>
technologies</div>
</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
